# Codex diff gate — I-beatboth-fix-000 (#1171) RETRIEVAL-BREADTH cluster (BB-001..BB-007)

Review the retrieval-breadth cluster fix (BB-001..BB-007 from outputs/vm_forensic/FIX_DESIGNS.json). Every fix is DISCOVERY-ONLY: candidates still flow through the unchanged fetch -> strict_verify -> entailment-judge/NLI -> 4-role seam chokepoint. None should touch a verification path. Files: scope_query_validator.py (BB-001 containment measure), live_retriever.py (BB-002 serper stop-on-zero-new, BB-004 s2 zero-yield telemetry, BB-007 unpaywall placeholder guard, storm_seed label), domain_backends.py (BB-003 openalex cursor paging), agentic_url_harvester.py (BB-006 harvest_storm_urls), run_honest_sweep_r3.py (BB-005 harvest/fetch decouple, BB-006 STORM ingest + seed lane), run_gate_b.py (slate + force-exact + BB-001 preflight), plus the new offline test file.

## VERIFY (line-by-line, against the staged diff below)

(a) **Every fix is DISCOVERY-ONLY** — strict_verify, the entailment judge/NLI, and the 4-role seam are byte-unchanged. The 10 verification-gate files (provenance_generator.py, entailment_judge.py, nli_verifier.py, strict_verify.py, role_pipeline.py, sentinel_adapter.py, judge_adapter.py, sweep_integration.py, native_gate_b_inputs.py, evaluator_gate.py) are NOT in this diff and are SHA-confirmed byte-identical to baseline. Grep the call sites in the diff: confirm no fix writes into the evidence pool any text other than fetched-then-verified candidate content, and no fix calls into or modifies a verification path.

(b) **Each flag defaults OFF (byte-identical) and the Gate-B slate activates it.** Verify each: PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE default "jaccard" == legacy; PG_AMPLIFIER_SCOPE_FLOOR default 0.15 == legacy; PG_SERPER_STOP_ON_ZERO_NEW default 0 == legacy short-page break; PG_OPENALEX_PER_PAGE default 25 + PG_OPENALEX_MAX_PAGES default 1 == legacy single-page min(limit,25) with NO cursor param sent; PG_AGENTIC_HARVEST_CAP default == fetch cap (no extra harvest); PG_STORM_INGEST_WEB_RESULTS default 0 == no STORM seeds; PG_UNPAYWALL_EMAIL placeholder == resolver no-ops. Then confirm _FULL_CAPABILITY_BENCHMARK_SLATE sets the ON value for each, and the force-exact / force-on sets cover the string/sub-1-float flags (the 0.08 float must NOT int()-truncate to 0 and silently disable the gate).

(c) **BB-006 ingests ONLY STORM web_results/academic_results URLs as candidates, NEVER the synthesized answer/key_findings/snippet (FAITHFULNESS-CRITICAL).** Read harvest_storm_urls in agentic_url_harvester.py line-by-line: confirm it reads ONLY rec["url"] from the web_results/academic_results streams, never answer/key_findings/outline/conversation/snippet text. Confirm the run_honest_sweep_r3.py BB-006 block fetches these URLs via run_live_retrieval(seed_only=True) so they pass through fetch -> strict_verify -> 4-role verbatim like any candidate (empty direct_quote), and that no STORM-synthesized text is merged into evidence. Any path that promotes STORM answer/key_findings into the evidence pool is a P0 fabrication path.

(d) **BB-001 KEEPS the gate (containment measure), does not remove it.** Confirm _containment(|q∩a|/min(|q|,|a|)) still drops genuinely off-anchor queries (the gate is reranking against intent), and the change only stops punishing short on-topic queries by anchor size. A fix that deletes the gate / sets the floor to 0 / always-keeps is a P1.

(e) **Pagination loops (BB-002 serper, BB-003 openalex) terminate correctly (no infinite loop) and dedup.** Serper: bounded by _n_pages; stops on budget met / 0-new-post-dedup / max pages; dedup by url (seen set). OpenAlex: bounded `for _page in range(max_pages)`; breaks on no-data / no-results / no-next-cursor / len>=limit; dedup by work id across pages. Confirm neither can loop forever and neither double-counts.

(f) **The offline smoke actually proves the funnel deltas** (not a tautology / not a string-presence check). Read the new test file: confirm each BB test asserts the actual count delta (containment keeps more than jaccard on a short-query/large-anchor fixture; serper fetches page 2 then stops on zero-new; openalex per_page=200 + cursor accumulates >25; s2 zero-yield surfaced; harvest_storm_urls returns ONLY url and NEVER answer/key_findings text; agentic harvest cap honored with dedup; unpaywall placeholder guard skips/fires), and that the OFF path is asserted byte-identical.

End with 'verdict: APPROVE' or 'verdict: REQUEST_CHANGES' then the schema:

```yaml
verdict: APPROVE | REQUEST_CHANGES
novel_p0: [...]
continuing_p0: [...]
p1: [...]
p2: [...]
convergence_call: continue | accept_remaining
remaining_blockers_for_execution: [...]
```

```diff
+def harvest_storm_urls(
+    storm_result: dict[str, Any] | None,
+    cap: int = 200,
+) -> list[str]:
+    """BB-006 (I-beatboth-fix-000 #1171): return ONLY the discovered URLs from a STORM
+    ``run_storm_interviews`` result — the EXACT analogue of ``harvest_agentic_urls``.
+
+    STORM grounds its multi-perspective interviews in REAL internet search results. Those
+    URLs (``storm_result["web_results"]`` then ``["academic_results"]``, each a dict with
+    ``url``/``title``/``snippet``) are legitimate candidate sources — but the run previously
+    DISCARDED them, only re-using STORM's synthesized interview QUESTIONS as query strings.
+
+    HARD URL-ONLY CONTRACT (faithfulness): this reads ONLY ``rec["url"]``. It NEVER reads the
+    STORM-synthesized ``answer`` / ``key_findings`` / outline / conversation text, and NEVER
+    the per-record ``snippet`` — promoting any LLM-synthesized STORM text into the evidence
+    pool would be a fabrication path. The harvested URLs are then fetched VERBATIM by
+    ``live_retriever.run_live_retrieval(seed_urls=…, seed_only=True)`` and gated by
+    strict_verify + the 4-role seam exactly like every other candidate (empty direct_quote).
+
+    Order-preserving + DETERMINISTIC; de-duplicates by ``canonical_source_url`` but RETURNS the
+    original fetchable URL. Returns at most ``cap`` URLs. Robust to missing/empty keys (returns
+    ``[]`` rather than raising). ``cap <= 0`` -> ``[]``.
+    """
+    if cap <= 0:
+        return []
+    result = storm_result or {}
+    seen_canonical: set[str] = set()
+    out: list[str] = []
+
+    def _consider(raw: Any) -> None:
+        if len(out) >= cap:
+            return
+        url = (raw or "").strip() if isinstance(raw, str) else ""
+        if not url:
+            return
+        try:
+            key = canonical_source_url(url) or url
+        except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — a malformed URL must not abort discovery
+            key = url
+        if key in seen_canonical:
+            return
+        seen_canonical.add(key)
+        out.append(url)
+
+    # Ordered result streams (deterministic). URL key ONLY — never answer/key_findings/snippet.
+    for stream_key in ("web_results", "academic_results"):
+        for rec in result.get(stream_key, []) or []:
+            if len(out) >= cap:
+                return out
+            if isinstance(rec, dict):
+                _consider(rec.get("url"))
+    return out
+

+def _openalex_per_page(limit: int) -> int:
+    """BB-003 (#1171): per-page size for the OpenAlex /works search.
+
+    Capped at the OpenAlex API maximum (200). DEFAULT 25 (PG_OPENALEX_PER_PAGE
+    unset) = byte-identical to the legacy ``max(1, min(limit, 25))``. The Gate-B
+    slate sets PG_OPENALEX_PER_PAGE=200 so one page covers up to 200 works.
+    A bad value FAILS LOUD (LAW II) rather than silently throttling to a default.
+    """
+    raw = os.getenv("PG_OPENALEX_PER_PAGE", "25").strip()
+    try:
+        cap = int(raw)
+    except ValueError:
+        raise ValueError(f"PG_OPENALEX_PER_PAGE={raw!r} is not an int")
+    cap = max(1, min(cap, _OPENALEX_PER_PAGE_MAX))
+    return max(1, min(limit, cap))
+
+
+def _openalex_max_pages() -> int:
+    """BB-003 (#1171): cursor-page count cap. DEFAULT 1 (PG_OPENALEX_MAX_PAGES
+    unset) = single page = byte-identical OFF. The slate raises it to cover the
+    requested ``limit``. A bad value FAILS LOUD."""
+    raw = os.getenv("PG_OPENALEX_MAX_PAGES", "1").strip()
+    try:
+        pages = int(raw)
+    except ValueError:
+        raise ValueError(f"PG_OPENALEX_MAX_PAGES={raw!r} is not an int")
+    return max(1, pages)

+def _containment(a: set[str], b: set[str]) -> float:
+    """Containment / overlap-coefficient similarity |a∩b| / min(|a|, |b|).
+
+    BB-001 (I-beatboth-fix-000 #1171): the symmetric Jaccard punishes a SHORT
+    on-topic query against a LARGE anchor bag — a 4-6-token query has a tiny
+    intersection over a huge union, so its sim sits far below the floor and the
+    query is dropped before it ever issues a search (the #1 retrieval-breadth
+    chokepoint: 40->5 kept on drb_72). Containment normalises by the SMALLER set,
+    so a short query whose tokens are all in the anchor scores ~1.0 while a query
+    that drifts off-anchor still scores low — it KEEPS the gate (reranks against
+    intent) rather than removing it. Empty a or b -> 0.0; never raises.
+    """
+    if not a or not b:
+        return 0.0
+    inter = a & b
+    smaller = min(len(a), len(b))
+    return len(inter) / smaller if smaller else 0.0
+
+
+# BB-001 (I-beatboth-fix-000 #1171): the default is `jaccard` so the OFF path is
+# BYTE-IDENTICAL to the pre-fix behaviour; the Gate-B slate sets `containment`.
+_SIM_MEASURES = {"jaccard": _jaccard, "containment": _containment}
+
+
+def _select_sim_measure():
+    """Return the (name, fn) for the configured similarity measure.
+
+    Reads ``PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE`` (default ``jaccard`` = byte-identical OFF).
+    An unrecognised value FAILS LOUD (LAW II) — a typo'd measure must not
+    silently fall back to a different gate behaviour on a paid benchmark run.
+    """
+    raw = os.getenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", "jaccard").strip().lower()
+    if raw not in _SIM_MEASURES:
+        raise ValueError(
+            f"PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE={raw!r} is not a recognised similarity measure "
+            f"(expected one of {sorted(_SIM_MEASURES)})."
+        )
+    return raw, _SIM_MEASURES[raw]
+
+

+        sim_name, floor, len(kept), len(dropped), len(anchor_tokens),
     )
     if dropped:
         sample = dropped[:3]

+"""I-beatboth-fix-000 (#1171) — RETRIEVAL BREADTH-COLLAPSE chain — offline funnel-delta smokes.
+
+Each test asserts ONE sub-fix's discovery-funnel widening AND that the default-OFF path is
+byte-identical. ALL OFFLINE (no network): the HTTP/agentic/STORM seams are stubbed. None of these
+fixes touch strict_verify, the entailment/NLI judge, or the 4-role seam — every test here is purely
+DISCOVERY-breadth (candidates) or telemetry/observability.
+
+  BB-001  scope-validator: containment keeps short on-topic queries that jaccard drops; OFF identical.
+  BB-002  Serper page loop: PG_SERPER_STOP_ON_ZERO_NEW continues past a sub-per_page page; OFF identical.
+  BB-003  OpenAlex search: cursor paging accumulates across pages > the legacy 25; OFF single page.
+  BB-004  Semantic Scholar: a HTTP-200 zero-yield traces a DISTINCT ok_zero/zero_yield (not silent ok).
+  BB-005  agentic harvest: harvest cap decoupled from fetch cap (discovery telemetry only).
+  BB-006  STORM web_results: harvest_storm_urls returns ONLY web_results[*].url, NEVER synthesized text.
+  BB-007  OA resolver: placeholder PG_UNPAYWALL_EMAIL -> resolver-unavailable trace (no silent no-op).
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import logging
+
+import pytest
+
+import src.polaris_graph.retrieval.domain_backends as db
+import src.polaris_graph.retrieval.live_retriever as lr

+    harvest_agentic_urls,
+    harvest_storm_urls,

+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+# BB-001 — scope-validator containment vs jaccard
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+
+def _wide_anchor_protocol() -> dict:
+    """A ~30-token anchor (research_question + PICO) — the size that punishes short
+    on-topic queries under symmetric Jaccard (tiny intersection / huge union)."""
+    return {
+        "research_question": (
+            "To what extent will artificial intelligence and automation technologies "
+            "displace or transform jobs across the labor market over the next decade, "
+            "and what does the empirical economics literature conclude about net "
+            "employment effects and wage polarization in advanced economies?"
+        ),
+        "population": "workers in advanced economies",
+        "intervention": "artificial intelligence automation",
+        "outcome": "employment wages displacement",
+    }
+
+
+# Eight SHORT (4-6 token) on-topic queries — each shares a few anchor terms but its
+# union with the 30-token anchor is huge, so jaccard sits far under any sane floor.
+_SHORT_ONTOPIC = [
+    "automation employment effects",
+    "artificial intelligence labor market",
+    "wage polarization advanced economies",
+    "job displacement automation decade",
+    "net employment effects automation",
+    "labor market transformation technology",
+    "economics literature automation jobs",
+    "ai workers displacement wages",
+]
+
+
+def test_bb001_containment_keeps_short_ontopic_where_jaccard_drops(monkeypatch):
+    """At the legacy code-default floor 0.15 (the forensic's chokepoint: "floor=0.15 kept=5
+    dropped=35"), symmetric jaccard drops the short on-topic queries (all score 0.067-0.143 < 0.15
+    against the 28-token anchor) while containment keeps them. Funnel delta: jaccard <=2 kept,
+    containment >=7 kept — the #1 retrieval-breadth chokepoint widened."""
+    proto = _wide_anchor_protocol()
+    floor = 0.15  # the legacy code default — the exact floor the forensic recorded the collapse at
+
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", "jaccard")
+    jac = validate_amplified_queries(list(_SHORT_ONTOPIC), proto, floor=floor)
+    # research_question is always prepended (always_keep_anchor); count only the 8 amplified.
+    jac_kept = [q for q in jac.kept if q in _SHORT_ONTOPIC]
+
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", "containment")
+    con = validate_amplified_queries(list(_SHORT_ONTOPIC), proto, floor=floor)
+    con_kept = [q for q in con.kept if q in _SHORT_ONTOPIC]
+
+    assert len(jac_kept) <= 2, f"jaccard should drop most short on-topic queries, kept {jac_kept}"
+    assert len(con_kept) >= 7, f"containment should keep short on-topic queries, kept {con_kept}"
+
+
+def test_bb001_off_default_is_jaccard_byte_identical(monkeypatch):
+    """Unset PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE == explicit jaccard == legacy behaviour (kept/dropped identical)."""
+    proto = _wide_anchor_protocol()
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", raising=False)
+    default = validate_amplified_queries(list(_SHORT_ONTOPIC), proto, floor=0.08)
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", "jaccard")
+    explicit = validate_amplified_queries(list(_SHORT_ONTOPIC), proto, floor=0.08)
+    assert default.kept == explicit.kept
+    # OFF reason string carries NO measure suffix (byte-identical legacy reason).
+    assert all(r.startswith("below_scope_floor_") and not r.endswith("jaccard")
+               for _q, _s, r in default.dropped)
+
+
+def test_bb001_containment_still_drops_genuine_drift(monkeypatch):
+    """The gate is KEPT, not removed: off-anchor drift still fails under containment."""
+    proto = _wide_anchor_protocol()
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", "containment")
+    drift = ["Japan national health insurance elderly care", "blockchain agriculture supply chain"]
+    res = validate_amplified_queries(drift, proto, floor=0.08)
+    dropped_q = [d[0] for d in res.dropped]
+    assert any("Japan" in q for q in dropped_q)
+    assert any("blockchain" in q for q in dropped_q)
+
+
+def test_bb001_unrecognised_measure_fails_loud(monkeypatch):
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", "cosine")
+    with pytest.raises(ValueError):
+        validate_amplified_queries(["x y z"], _wide_anchor_protocol(), floor=0.08)
+

+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+# BB-002 — Serper page loop (stop-on-zero-new)
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+
+def _install_serper_pages(monkeypatch, pages: dict[int, list[str]]):
+    calls: list[int] = []
+
+    def _fake(query, per_page, page, headers):
+        calls.append(page)
+        urls = pages.get(page, [])
+        items = [{"url": u, "title": "t", "snippet": "s", "source": "serper"} for u in urls]
+        return items, True, 1.0, 100, ""
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(lr, "_serper_fetch_page", _fake)
+    monkeypatch.setenv("SERPER_API_KEY", "test-key")
+    return calls
+
+
+def test_bb002_stop_on_zero_new_continues_past_short_page(monkeypatch):
+    """With the flag ON, a sub-per_page page that adds NEW urls does NOT stop the loop."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_STOP_ON_ZERO_NEW", "1")
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_TOTAL_PER_QUERY", "60")
+    # page 1: only 5 urls (< per_page 20) but all NEW -> must continue; page 2: 8 more NEW.
+    calls = _install_serper_pages(monkeypatch, {
+        1: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(5)],
+        2: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(5, 13)],
+        3: [],  # zero new -> stop
+    })
+    out = lr._serper_search("q", num=20)
+    assert calls == [1, 2, 3], f"expected to page past the short page, got {calls}"
+    assert len(out) == 13
+
+
+def test_bb002_stop_on_zero_new_stops_on_duplicate_page(monkeypatch):
+    """A page that adds 0 NEW (all duplicates) stops the loop even with budget remaining."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_STOP_ON_ZERO_NEW", "1")
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_TOTAL_PER_QUERY", "200")
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_MAX_PAGES", "5")
+    calls = _install_serper_pages(monkeypatch, {
+        1: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(20)],
+        2: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(20)],  # all duplicates -> 0 new -> stop
+        3: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(40, 60)],  # never reached
+    })
+    out = lr._serper_search("q", num=20)
+    assert calls == [1, 2], f"duplicate page should stop the loop, got {calls}"
+    assert len(out) == 20
+
+
+def test_bb002_off_default_short_page_stops_byte_identical(monkeypatch):
+    """OFF (default): a sub-per_page page-1 stops immediately — the legacy FX-17 behaviour."""
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_SERPER_STOP_ON_ZERO_NEW", raising=False)
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_TOTAL_PER_QUERY", "60")
+    calls = _install_serper_pages(monkeypatch, {
+        1: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(5)],
+        2: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(5, 13)],  # would be reached only if the flag were on
+    })
+    out = lr._serper_search("q", num=20)
+    assert calls == [1], f"OFF must stop on the short page (legacy), got {calls}"
+    assert len(out) == 5
+
+
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+# BB-003 — OpenAlex cursor paging
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+
+def _make_oa_works(start: int, n: int) -> list[dict]:
+    return [
+        {"id": f"https://openalex.org/W{i}", "doi": "", "display_name": f"work {i}",
+         "publication_year": 2023}
+        for i in range(start, start + n)
+    ]
+
+
+def test_bb003_cursor_paging_accumulates_past_25(monkeypatch):
+    """With per_page=200 + max_pages>1, the cursor loop accumulates across pages (> the legacy 25)."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_OPENALEX_PER_PAGE", "200")
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_OPENALEX_MAX_PAGES", "3")
+    seen_params: list[dict] = []
+    pages = {
+        "*": {"results": _make_oa_works(0, 200), "meta": {"next_cursor": "c2"}},
+        "c2": {"results": _make_oa_works(200, 200), "meta": {"next_cursor": "c3"}},
+        "c3": {"results": _make_oa_works(400, 50), "meta": {"next_cursor": None}},
+    }
+
+    def _fake_get_json(url, params=None):
+        seen_params.append(dict(params or {}))
+        return pages.get((params or {}).get("cursor"), {"results": [], "meta": {}})
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(db, "_http_get_json", _fake_get_json)
+    # limit=450 so the loop must consume all 3 cursor pages (200+200+50) to accumulate past 25.
+    out = db.openalex_search("automation labor", limit=450)
+    assert len(out) == 450, f"cursor loop should accumulate across pages, got {len(out)}"
+    assert len(out) > 25, "BB-003: must accumulate well past the legacy 25/query single-page cap"
+    # per_page=200 sent (the OpenAlex max), and the cursor param threaded across all 3 pages.
+    assert all(p["per_page"] == 200 for p in seen_params)
+    assert seen_params[0]["cursor"] == "*"
+    assert len(seen_params) == 3
+    assert [p["cursor"] for p in seen_params] == ["*", "c2", "c3"]
+
+
+def test_bb003_off_default_single_page_no_cursor_byte_identical(monkeypatch):
+    """OFF (per_page unset=25, max_pages unset=1): exactly the legacy single 25-cap request, no cursor."""
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_OPENALEX_PER_PAGE", raising=False)
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_OPENALEX_MAX_PAGES", raising=False)
+    seen_params: list[dict] = []
+
+    def _fake_get_json(url, params=None):
+        seen_params.append(dict(params or {}))
+        return {"results": _make_oa_works(0, 25), "meta": {"next_cursor": "c2"}}
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(db, "_http_get_json", _fake_get_json)
+    out = db.openalex_search("automation labor", limit=100)
+    assert len(seen_params) == 1, "OFF must issue exactly one page"
+    assert "cursor" not in seen_params[0], "OFF request must NOT carry a cursor param (byte-identical)"
+    assert seen_params[0]["per_page"] == 25  # max(1, min(100, 25))
+    assert len(out) == 25
+
+
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+# BB-004 — Semantic Scholar zero-yield loud signal
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+
+class _FakeResp:
+    def __init__(self, status_code, payload):
+        self.status_code = status_code
+        self._payload = payload
+        self.content = b"{}"
+
+    def json(self):
+        return self._payload
+
+
+class _FakeClient:
+    def __init__(self, *a, **k):
+        pass
+
+    def __enter__(self):
+        return self
+
+    def __exit__(self, *a):
+        return False
+
+
+def _install_s2(monkeypatch, payload):
+    traced: list[dict] = []
+
+    def _fake_get(self, url, params=None, headers=None):
+        return _FakeResp(200, payload)
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(_FakeClient, "get", _fake_get, raising=False)
+    monkeypatch.setattr(lr.httpx, "Client", lambda *a, **k: _FakeClient())
+
+    def _fake_trace(tool_name, **kw):
+        if tool_name == "s2":
+            traced.append({"tool": tool_name, **kw})
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(lr, "_trace_tool", _fake_trace)
+    monkeypatch.setattr(lr, "_trace_query", lambda *a, **k: None)
+    return traced
+
+
+def test_bb004_zero_yield_traces_distinct_signal(monkeypatch):
+    """A HTTP-200 with 0 usable papers traces status=ok_zero + zero_yield=True (NOT silent ok)."""
+    traced = _install_s2(monkeypatch, {"data": []})
+    out = lr._s2_bulk_search("metformin", limit=12)
+    assert out == []
+    s2_row = traced[-1]
+    assert s2_row["status"] == "ok_zero", f"zero-yield must trace ok_zero, got {s2_row['status']}"
+    assert s2_row["zero_yield"] is True
+    assert s2_row["result_count"] == 0
+
+
+def test_bb004_nonzero_yield_stays_ok(monkeypatch):
+    """A normal yield stays status=ok with zero_yield=False (byte-identical success semantics)."""
+    payload = {"data": [
+        {"title": "p", "abstract": "a", "openAccessPdf": {"url": "https://oa/p.pdf"},
+         "externalIds": {"DOI": "10.1/x"}, "paperId": "P1", "year": 2023, "venue": "v"},
+    ]}
+    traced = _install_s2(monkeypatch, payload)
+    out = lr._s2_bulk_search("metformin", limit=12)
+    assert len(out) == 1
+    s2_row = traced[-1]
+    assert s2_row["status"] == "ok"
+    assert s2_row["zero_yield"] is False
+    assert s2_row["result_count"] == 1
+
+
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+# BB-005 — agentic harvest cap honored (decoupled from fetch)
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+
+def _agentic_result_with(n: int) -> dict:
+    return {"web_results": [{"url": f"https://a/{i}", "title": "t", "snippet": "s"} for i in range(n)]}
+
+
+def test_bb005_harvest_cap_honored_dedup_intact():
+    """harvest_agentic_urls(result_with_1933, cap=800) returns 800 (the raised discovery cap)."""
+    res = _agentic_result_with(1933)
+    out = harvest_agentic_urls(res, cap=800)
+    assert len(out) == 800
+    assert len(set(out)) == 800  # dedup intact
+
+
+def test_bb005_harvest_cap_smaller_than_discovered_truncates():
+    """The fetch cap (100) truncates the harvested set — the budget-respecting fetch subset."""
+    res = _agentic_result_with(1933)
+    out = harvest_agentic_urls(res, cap=100)
+    assert len(out) == 100
+
+
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+# BB-006 — STORM URL-ONLY harvest (faithfulness contract)
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+
+def _storm_out_with(n: int) -> dict:
+    """A STORM result carrying web_results URLs AND synthesized text that must NEVER be harvested."""
+    return {
+        "storm_conversations": [{"q": "interview q", "a": "interview answer text"}],
+        "storm_outline": ["section 1", "section 2"],
+        "web_results": [
+            {"url": f"https://storm/{i}", "title": f"title {i}",
+             "snippet": f"SYNTHESIZED-SNIPPET-{i}-must-not-be-evidence"}
+            for i in range(n)
+        ],
+        "academic_results": [{"url": f"https://storm-ac/{i}", "title": "ac", "snippet": "ac snip"}
+                             for i in range(3)],
+        # synthesized fields that must NEVER appear in the harvest:
+        "answer": "STORM SYNTHESIZED ANSWER — this is a paraphrase and must not be evidence",
+        "key_findings": ["STORM KEY FINDING that is an LLM paraphrase"],
+    }
+
+
+def test_bb006_harvest_storm_urls_returns_only_urls():
+    """harvest_storm_urls returns ONLY web_results/academic_results URLs — never synthesized text."""
+    out = harvest_storm_urls(_storm_out_with(478), cap=200)
+    assert len(out) == 200  # capped
+    # Every returned item is a fetchable URL from the result streams.
+    assert all(u.startswith("https://storm") for u in out)
+    # The HARD contract: no synthesized STORM text leaked into the harvest.
+    blob = " ".join(out)
+    assert "SYNTHESIZED-SNIPPET" not in blob
+    assert "SYNTHESIZED ANSWER" not in blob
+    assert "KEY FINDING" not in blob
+    assert "interview answer" not in blob
+
+
+def test_bb006_harvest_storm_urls_deduped_and_capped():
+    out = harvest_storm_urls(_storm_out_with(50), cap=200)
+    assert len(out) == len(set(out))      # deduped
+    assert len(out) == 53                 # 50 web + 3 academic, all distinct
+
+
+def test_bb006_harvest_storm_urls_empty_safe():
+    assert harvest_storm_urls(None, cap=200) == []
+    assert harvest_storm_urls({}, cap=200) == []
+    assert harvest_storm_urls(_storm_out_with(10), cap=0) == []
+
+
+def test_bb006_storm_snippet_never_becomes_direct_quote():
+    """A STORM seed URL flows as a URL-only candidate: harvest never carries the snippet as a quote.
+
+    (The seed re-fetch makes direct_quote the verbatim FETCHED span; the harvest output is a bare
+    URL string — there is no field through which the synthesized snippet could ride as evidence.)
+    """
+    out = harvest_storm_urls(_storm_out_with(5), cap=200)
+    assert all(isinstance(u, str) and u.startswith("http") for u in out)
+
+
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+# BB-007 — OA resolver placeholder-email guard
+# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+
+def test_bb007_placeholder_email_traces_resolver_unavailable(monkeypatch):
+    """The placeholder PG_UNPAYWALL_EMAIL -> resolver-unavailable trace + [] (no silent no-op)."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_UNPAYWALL_EMAIL", "polaris@example.org")
+    traced: list[dict] = []
+    monkeypatch.setattr(lr, "_trace_tool",
+                        lambda tool, **kw: traced.append({"tool": tool, **kw}))
+
+    def _boom_client(*a, **k):
+        raise AssertionError("Unpaywall must NOT be called with the placeholder email")
+    monkeypatch.setattr(lr.httpx, "Client", _boom_client)
+
+    out = lr._unpaywall_get_oa_urls("10.1056/NEJMoa2307563")
+    assert out == []
+    oa_rows = [t for t in traced if t["tool"] == "oa_resolver"]
+    assert oa_rows, "expected an oa_resolver trace row"
+    assert oa_rows[-1]["status"] == "unavailable"
+    assert oa_rows[-1].get("resolver_unavailable") is True
+    assert oa_rows[-1].get("error") == "placeholder_unpaywall_email"
+
+
+def test_bb007_empty_email_also_unavailable(monkeypatch):
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_UNPAYWALL_EMAIL", "")
+    monkeypatch.setattr(lr, "_trace_tool", lambda *a, **k: None)
+    monkeypatch.setattr(lr.httpx, "Client",
+                        lambda *a, **k: (_ for _ in ()).throw(AssertionError("no call")))
+    assert lr._unpaywall_get_oa_urls("10.1/x") == []
+
+
+def test_bb007_real_email_resolves_stubbed(monkeypatch):
+    """A REAL email lets the resolver fire; with a stubbed OA response it returns the OA url(s)."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_UNPAYWALL_EMAIL", "research@polaris-dr.org")
+    monkeypatch.setattr(lr, "_trace_tool", lambda *a, **k: None)
+
+    class _Resp:
+        status_code = 200
+
+        def json(self):
+            return {"is_oa": True, "best_oa_location": {"url_for_pdf": "https://oa/full.pdf"}}
+
+    class _Client:
+        def __init__(self, *a, **k):
+            pass
+
+        def __enter__(self):
+            return self
+
+        def __exit__(self, *a):
+            return False
+
+        def get(self, *a, **k):
+            return _Resp()
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(lr.httpx, "Client", lambda *a, **k: _Client())
+    # Stub the shared parser to the canonical OA-URL shape.
+    import src.polaris_graph.retrieval.frame_fetcher as ff
+    monkeypatch.setattr(
+        ff, "_parse_unpaywall_response",
+        lambda d: {"is_oa": True, "oa_pdf_url": "https://oa/full.pdf", "oa_html_url": ""},
+    )
+    out = lr._unpaywall_get_oa_urls("10.1056/NEJMoa2307563")
+    assert out == ["https://oa/full.pdf"]
+

+def test_bb007_openalex_search_doi_threads_to_candidate_metadata(monkeypatch):
+    """BB-007 part-2 regression: an openalex_search candidate WITH a DOI carries it in metadata
+    AND its URL is doi.org — so _candidate_oa_hints + _extract_doi_from_url both surface the DOI to
+    the OA resolver. (A DOI-less work gets an openalex.org/W url with metadata['doi']=None; there is
+    genuinely no DOI to thread, so the resolver correctly cannot fire — not a bug.)"""
+    def _fake_get_json(url, params=None):
+        return {"results": [
+            {"id": "https://openalex.org/W1", "doi": "https://doi.org/10.1/withdoi",
+             "display_name": "has doi", "publication_year": 2023},
+            {"id": "https://openalex.org/W2", "doi": "", "display_name": "no doi",
+             "publication_year": 2022},
+        ], "meta": {}}
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(db, "_http_get_json", _fake_get_json)
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_OPENALEX_PER_PAGE", raising=False)
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_OPENALEX_MAX_PAGES", raising=False)
+    out = db.openalex_search("q", limit=10)
+    by_title = {c.title: c for c in out}
+    # WITH-doi candidate: url is doi.org AND metadata carries the DOI -> resolver can fire.
+    with_doi = by_title["has doi"]
+    assert with_doi.url.startswith("https://doi.org/")
+    assert with_doi.metadata["doi"] == "https://doi.org/10.1/withdoi"
+    assert lr._candidate_oa_hints(with_doi.metadata)[0] == "https://doi.org/10.1/withdoi"
+    # NO-doi candidate: openalex.org/W url, metadata doi None -> genuinely no DOI to thread.
+    no_doi = by_title["no doi"]
+    assert no_doi.url.startswith("https://openalex.org/W")
+    assert no_doi.metadata["doi"] is None
+    assert lr._candidate_oa_hints(no_doi.metadata)[0] == ""

```

src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:1157:13. **Policy-scope disambiguation (M-NEW-1, GH#422)**: When a paragraph names a specific program (Bill C-64, ACA, MACRA, EU AI Act, Article 34.7 CUSMA review, a particular budget line, etc.) and the evidence pool also contains projections / cost estimates / impact analyses for a RELATED-BUT-BROADER scope (universal single-payer projection vs phase-1 narrow program; comprehensive coverage estimate vs narrow amendment; multi-jurisdiction equivalent of a single-state rule), do NOT silently fold the broader projection into the narrow-program paragraph. When citing numbers from the broader scope, EXPLICITLY label the scope-attribution INLINE in the SAME sentence as the citation. Required pattern: write "PBO 2023 universal single-payer projection estimates the additional cost at $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_X]" — NOT "the incremental cost is $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_X]" inside a paragraph that opens with Bill C-64 phase-1 (which covers only contraception and diabetes medications). The decimal and the citation are correct; the missing scope label is what makes the conflation. Same evidence-ID, additional 4-8 word scope phrase before the citation. This rule fires regardless of which section the named-program paragraph appears in (Regulatory, Comparative, Economic, etc.). Failure mode this rule prevents: a reader concludes a narrow program will cost the broader program's projected figure. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "Bill C-64 covers a defined set of contraception and diabetes medications [ev_A]. The PBO's 2023 cost estimate of a universal single-payer drug plan modeled on an expanded Quebec formulary projects incremental public-sector cost of $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_B]." — distinct scopes named, decimals attributed to broader scope. BAD: "Under Bill C-64, the incremental cost to the public sector is estimated at $11.2 billion in 2024-25 [ev_B]." — cites the PBO universal-plan source as if it were a Bill C-64 phase-1 projection.

 2761:         class _LiveContentParallelFetcher:
 2762:             """Adapter wrapping `_fetch_content(url, max_chars)` for
 2763:             the parallel_fetch substrate's ParallelFetcher Protocol.
 2764:             Stashes the full 5-tuple (content, ok, title, body_type, jsonld)
 2765:             in a thread-safe side dict so the post-processing loop
 2766:             can read it back per-candidate."""
 2767: 
 2768:             def __init__(self, max_chars: int) -> None:
 2769:                 self.max_chars = max_chars
 2770:                 self._lock = threading.Lock()
 2771:                 self.results = fetched_side
 2772: 
 2773:             def fetch(
 2774:                 self, task: "FetchTask"
 2775:             ) -> tuple[bytes, str, int]:
 2776:                 # I-meta-007c: surface the per-candidate DOI/PMID hints
 2777:                 # (stashed in task_metadata at task construction) so the OA
 2778:                 # resolver can fire on the DEFAULT parallel path, not just the
 2779:                 # serial fallback.
 2780:                 _meta = task.task_metadata or {}
 2781:                 content, ok, title, body_type, jsonld = _fetch_content(
 2782:                     task.source_url, self.max_chars,
 2783:                     doi_hint=str(_meta.get("doi") or ""),
 2784:                     pmid_hint=str(_meta.get("pmid") or ""),
 2785:                 )
 2786:                 with self._lock:
 2787:                     self.results[task.source_url] = (
 2788:                         content, ok, title, body_type, jsonld,
 2789:                     )
 2790:                 payload = (content or "").encode("utf-8", errors="replace")
 2791:                 return (payload, "text/plain", 200 if ok else 502)

 succeeded in 17472ms:
    1: """I-cap-002 feature 3/4 (#1060): harvest DISCOVERED URLs from an agentic-search result + a pure
    2: seed-URL evidence merge core.
    3: 
    4: The agentic loop (``agents/searcher.execute_agentic_search``) is used in the benchmark for **URL
    5: DISCOVERY ONLY**. Its LLM-written page summaries (``agentic_research_notebook``) must NEVER become
    6: evidence — POLARIS's core invariant is verbatim-span faithfulness, and a model paraphrase masquerading
    7: as a ``direct_quote`` would be a fabrication. So we read ONLY the discovered URLs here; the discovered
    8: URLs are then fetched **verbatim** by ``live_retriever.run_live_retrieval(seed_urls=…, seed_only=True)``
    9: and verified by strict_verify + the 4-role seam, exactly like the rest of the corpus.
   10: 
   11: Three pure, stdlib-light functions (no network, no LLM, no new dependency):
   12: - ``harvest_agentic_urls`` — ordered, canonical-deduped, capped list of discovered URLs (originals).
   13: - ``harvest_storm_urls`` — BB-006 (#1171): the same URL-ONLY harvest applied to a STORM-interview
   14:   result's ``web_results`` / ``academic_results`` streams (the 478/540 interview search-result URLs the
   15:   benchmark previously discarded). NEVER reads STORM's synthesized answer/key_findings/snippet text.
   16: - ``merge_seed_url_evidence`` — the deepener's dedup-by-URL + global evidence-id renumber core, factored
   17:   out so it is unit-testable (and a future PR can repoint the deepener at it).
   18: """
   19: 
   20: from __future__ import annotations
   21: 
   22: from typing import Any
   23: 
   24: from src.polaris_graph.retrieval.saturation import canonical_source_url
   25: 
   26: 
   27: def harvest_agentic_urls(
   28:     agentic_result: dict[str, Any] | None,
   29:     cap: int = 200,
   30: ) -> list[str]:
   31:     """Return ONLY the discovered URLs from an ``execute_agentic_search`` result.
   32: 
   33:     Order-preserving and DETERMINISTIC: harvests from the ordered ``web_results`` then
   34:     ``academic_results`` streams first (these are the authoritative, complete, append-ordered streams —
   35:     incl. post-loop DDG / citation-chase URLs), then supplements with any ``agentic_url_accumulator``
   36:     entries not already seen. De-duplicates by ``canonical_source_url`` (scheme/tracking-stripped) but
   37:     RETURNS the original fetchable URL (canonical strings would hurt the live fetch yield). Returns at
   38:     most ``cap`` URLs. NEVER reads ``agentic_research_notebook`` / summaries / snippets. Robust to
   39:     missing/empty keys (returns ``[]`` rather than raising). ``cap <= 0`` → ``[]``.
   40:     """
   41:     if cap <= 0:
   42:         return []
   43:     result = agentic_result or {}
   44:     seen_canonical: set[str] = set()
   45:     out: list[str] = []
   46: 
   47:     def _consider(raw: Any) -> None:
   48:         if len(out) >= cap:
   49:             return
   50:         url = (raw or "").strip() if isinstance(raw, str) else ""
   51:         if not url:
   52:             return
   53:         try:
   54:             key = canonical_source_url(url) or url
   55:         except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — a malformed URL must not abort discovery
   56:             key = url
   57:         if key in seen_canonical:
   58:             return
   59:         seen_canonical.add(key)
   60:         out.append(url)
   61: 
   62:     # Ordered result streams first (deterministic, complete).
   63:     for stream_key in ("web_results", "academic_results"):
   64:         for rec in result.get(stream_key, []) or []:
   65:             if len(out) >= cap:
   66:                 return out
   67:             if isinstance(rec, dict):
   68:                 _consider(rec.get("url"))
   69:     # Supplement with the accumulator (subset; set-ordered, so appended last for completeness only).
   70:     for url in result.get("agentic_url_accumulator", []) or []:
   71:         if len(out) >= cap:
   72:             return out
   73:         _consider(url)
   74:     return out
   75: 
   76: 
   77: def harvest_storm_urls(
   78:     storm_result: dict[str, Any] | None,
   79:     cap: int = 200,
   80: ) -> list[str]:
   81:     """BB-006 (I-beatboth-fix-000 #1171): return ONLY the discovered URLs from a STORM
   82:     ``run_storm_interviews`` result — the EXACT analogue of ``harvest_agentic_urls``.
   83: 
   84:     STORM grounds its multi-perspective interviews in REAL internet search results. Those
   85:     URLs (``storm_result["web_results"]`` then ``["academic_results"]``, each a dict with
   86:     ``url``/``title``/``snippet``) are legitimate candidate sources — but the run previously
   87:     DISCARDED them, only re-using STORM's synthesized interview QUESTIONS as query strings.
   88: 
   89:     HARD URL-ONLY CONTRACT (faithfulness): this reads ONLY ``rec["url"]``. It NEVER reads the
   90:     STORM-synthesized ``answer`` / ``key_findings`` / outline / conversation text, and NEVER
   91:     the per-record ``snippet`` — promoting any LLM-synthesized STORM text into the evidence
   92:     pool would be a fabrication path. The harvested URLs are then fetched VERBATIM by
   93:     ``live_retriever.run_live_retrieval(seed_urls=…, seed_only=True)`` and gated by
   94:     strict_verify + the 4-role seam exactly like every other candidate (empty direct_quote).
   95: 
   96:     Order-preserving + DETERMINISTIC; de-duplicates by ``canonical_source_url`` but RETURNS the
   97:     original fetchable URL. Returns at most ``cap`` URLs. Robust to missing/empty keys (returns
   98:     ``[]`` rather than raising). ``cap <= 0`` -> ``[]``.
   99:     """
  100:     if cap <= 0:
  101:         return []
  102:     result = storm_result or {}
  103:     seen_canonical: set[str] = set()
  104:     out: list[str] = []
  105: 
  106:     def _consider(raw: Any) -> None:
  107:         if len(out) >= cap:
  108:             return
  109:         url = (raw or "").strip() if isinstance(raw, str) else ""
  110:         if not url:
  111:             return
  112:         try:
  113:             key = canonical_source_url(url) or url
  114:         except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — a malformed URL must not abort discovery
  115:             key = url
  116:         if key in seen_canonical:
  117:             return
  118:         seen_canonical.add(key)
  119:         out.append(url)
  120: 
  121:     # Ordered result streams (deterministic). URL key ONLY — never answer/key_findings/snippet.
  122:     for stream_key in ("web_results", "academic_results"):
  123:         for rec in result.get(stream_key, []) or []:
  124:             if len(out) >= cap:
  125:                 return out
  126:             if isinstance(rec, dict):
  127:                 _consider(rec.get("url"))
  128:     return out
  129: 
  130: 
  131: def merge_seed_url_evidence(
  132:     staged_sources: list[Any],
  133:     staged_rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
  134:     new_sources: list[Any],
  135:     new_rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
  136: ) -> tuple[list[Any], list[dict[str, Any]], int, int]:
  137:     """Dedup-by-URL source merge + global evidence-id renumber (the deepener's accepted-source core).
  138: 
  139:     - ``new_sources`` whose ``.url`` is not already among ``staged_sources`` are appended; their URLs
  140:       form the ACCEPTED set.
  141:     - Only ``new_rows`` whose source URL (``source_url`` or ``url``) is in the ACCEPTED set are
  142:       appended — so a duplicate source contributes NO rows (no evidence_row_count inflation).
  143:     - Appended rows get a fresh ``evidence_id`` = ``ev_{base + i:03d}`` from ``len(staged_rows)`` so ids
  144:       never collide/overwrite.
  145: 
  146:     Returns ``(merged_sources, merged_rows, accepted_source_count, accepted_row_count)``. Operates on
  147:     COPIES; the inputs are not mutated. No I/O.
  148:     """
  149:     merged_sources = list(staged_sources)
  150:     seen_urls = {getattr(s, "url", None) for s in merged_sources}
  151:     accepted_src_urls: set[str] = set()
  152:     accepted_sources = 0
  153:     for src in new_sources:
  154:         url = getattr(src, "url", None)
  155:         if url and url not in seen_urls:
  156:             seen_urls.add(url)
  157:             merged_sources.append(src)
  158:             accepted_src_urls.add(url)
  159:             accepted_sources += 1
  160: 
  161:     merged_rows = list(staged_rows)
  162:     base = len(merged_rows)
  163:     accepted_rows = 0
  164:     for ev in new_rows:
  165:         ev_url = (ev.get("source_url") or ev.get("url") or "").strip()
  166:         if not ev_url or ev_url not in accepted_src_urls:
  167:             continue  # duplicate / not an accepted source — skip (no inflation)
  168:         ev = dict(ev)  # copy so the caller's row object is not mutated
  169:         ev["evidence_id"] = f"ev_{base + accepted_rows:03d}"
  170:         merged_rows.append(ev)
  171:         accepted_rows += 1
  172: 
  173:     return merged_sources, merged_rows, accepted_sources, accepted_rows

 succeeded in 10228ms:
    1: """
    2: Scope-protocol query validator — HONEST-REBUILD Phase 2e.
    3: 
    4: Validates that amplified search queries stay within the pre-registered
    5: protocol's research scope. Drops queries that have drifted off-topic
    6: before they waste retrieval budget.
    7: 
    8: WHY THIS EXISTS (PG_LB_SA_02_CONTENT_AUDIT Section E-04):
    9: The pre-rebuild pipeline amplified a single research question into
   10: 10-25 search variants using an LLM. Some variants drifted:
   11:   original: "efficacy of semaglutide for weight loss"
   12:   amplified: "Japan national health insurance elderly care coverage"
   13: 
   14: These drifted queries pulled in the junk that Phase 2d's post-fetch
   15: off-topic filter then had to remove. Dropping drift at amplification
   16: time is cheaper than fetching and discarding.
   17: 
   18: DESIGN:
   19: - No new LLM call. Uses token overlap with protocol.research_question +
   20:   PICO fields (intervention / population / outcome) as the anchor.
   21: - Drops any amplified query whose similarity with the anchor is below
   22:   PG_AMPLIFIER_SCOPE_FLOOR (default 0.15).
   23: - ALWAYS keeps the verbatim research_question and direct PICO-term
   24:   queries ("{intervention} {population}") as a safety net.
   25: - Logs drops so the user can see which amplifier variants were killed.
   26: 
   27: SIMILARITY MEASURE (BB-001, I-beatboth-fix-000 #1171):
   28: - PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE selects the measure: `jaccard` (default = byte-identical
   29:   OFF) or `containment`. Symmetric Jaccard (|q∩a|/|q∪a|) punishes a SHORT
   30:   on-topic query against a large anchor bag (tiny intersection over a huge
   31:   union) — the #1 retrieval-breadth chokepoint (40->5 kept on drb_72).
   32:   Containment/overlap-coefficient (|q∩a|/min(|q|,|a|)) normalises by the
   33:   smaller set so a short on-topic query clears while genuine drift still fails.
   34:   The GATE is KEPT either way (rerank against intent); only the measure changes.
   35: """
   36: 
   37: from __future__ import annotations
   38: 
   39: import logging
   40: import os
   41: import re
   42: from dataclasses import dataclass
   43: from typing import Any, Optional
   44: 
   45: logger = logging.getLogger("polaris_graph.scope_query_validator")
   46: 
   47: 
   48: # Very small English stopword set — we care about domain terms, so
   49: # we strip only the grammatical connective tissue.
   50: _STOPWORDS = frozenset({
   51:     "a", "an", "and", "are", "as", "at", "be", "but", "by", "for", "from",
   52:     "has", "have", "in", "is", "it", "its", "of", "on", "or", "that",
   53:     "the", "this", "to", "was", "were", "will", "with", "what", "which",
   54:     "how", "why", "when", "where", "who", "whom", "whose", "i", "you",
   55:     "we", "they", "can", "could", "should", "would", "may", "might",
   56:     "do", "does", "did", "done", "being", "been", "about", "into",
   57:     "than", "then", "so", "also", "more", "most", "some", "any", "all",
   58:     "not", "no", "only", "very", "just", "other",
   59: })
   60: 
   61: _TOKEN_RE = re.compile(r"[A-Za-z][A-Za-z0-9\-]{1,}")
   62: 
   63: 
   64: def _tokenize(text: str) -> set[str]:
   65:     """Lowercased tokens minus stopwords, minus short tokens."""
   66:     if not text:
   67:         return set()
   68:     tokens = {
   69:         t.lower()
   70:         for t in _TOKEN_RE.findall(text)
   71:         if len(t) > 2
   72:     }
   73:     return tokens - _STOPWORDS
   74: 
   75: 
   76: def _jaccard(a: set[str], b: set[str]) -> float:
   77:     """Jaccard (symmetric) similarity |a∩b| / |a∪b|. Empty a or b -> 0.0."""
   78:     if not a or not b:
   79:         return 0.0
   80:     union = a | b
   81:     inter = a & b
   82:     return len(inter) / len(union) if union else 0.0
   83: 
   84: 
   85: def _containment(a: set[str], b: set[str]) -> float:
   86:     """Containment / overlap-coefficient similarity |a∩b| / min(|a|, |b|).
   87: 
   88:     BB-001 (I-beatboth-fix-000 #1171): the symmetric Jaccard punishes a SHORT
   89:     on-topic query against a LARGE anchor bag — a 4-6-token query has a tiny
   90:     intersection over a huge union, so its sim sits far below the floor and the
   91:     query is dropped before it ever issues a search (the #1 retrieval-breadth
   92:     chokepoint: 40->5 kept on drb_72). Containment normalises by the SMALLER set,
   93:     so a short query whose tokens are all in the anchor scores ~1.0 while a query
   94:     that drifts off-anchor still scores low — it KEEPS the gate (reranks against
   95:     intent) rather than removing it. Empty a or b -> 0.0; never raises.
   96:     """
   97:     if not a or not b:
   98:         return 0.0
   99:     inter = a & b
  100:     smaller = min(len(a), len(b))
  101:     return len(inter) / smaller if smaller else 0.0
  102: 
  103: 
  104: # BB-001 (I-beatboth-fix-000 #1171): the default is `jaccard` so the OFF path is
  105: # BYTE-IDENTICAL to the pre-fix behaviour; the Gate-B slate sets `containment`.
  106: _SIM_MEASURES = {"jaccard": _jaccard, "containment": _containment}
  107: 
  108: 
  109: def _select_sim_measure():
  110:     """Return the (name, fn) for the configured similarity measure.
  111: 
  112:     Reads ``PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE`` (default ``jaccard`` = byte-identical OFF).
  113:     An unrecognised value FAILS LOUD (LAW II) — a typo'd measure must not
  114:     silently fall back to a different gate behaviour on a paid benchmark run.
  115:     """
  116:     raw = os.getenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", "jaccard").strip().lower()
  117:     if raw not in _SIM_MEASURES:
  118:         raise ValueError(
  119:             f"PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE={raw!r} is not a recognised similarity measure "
  120:             f"(expected one of {sorted(_SIM_MEASURES)})."
  121:         )
  122:     return raw, _SIM_MEASURES[raw]
  123: 
  124:

  126: class ValidationResult:
  127:     """Return value of validate_amplified_queries()."""
  128: 
  129:     kept: list[str]
  130:     dropped: list[tuple[str, float, str]]  # (query, similarity, reason)
  131:     anchor_tokens_used: list[str]
  132: 
  133: 
  134: def _build_anchor_tokens(protocol: dict[str, Any]) -> set[str]:
  135:     """Merge research_question + anchor tokens into one anchor set.
  136: 
  137:     Accepts either a ProtocolDocument dict (from scope_gate) or any dict with
  138:     similar fields. Missing fields are skipped gracefully.
  139: 
  140:     Clinical PICO fields (population / intervention / comparator / outcome) are
  141:     string-valued and tokenized as before — OFF byte-identical.
  142: 
  143:     I-meta-005 Phase 1 (#985, brief §2.4): ADDITIVELY also merge the field-
  144:     agnostic `ResearchFrame` anchor fields (entities / relations / metrics /
  145:     comparators / constraints) when present, so planner sub-queries derived
  146:     from a non-clinical frame validate against the frame's OWN tokens. These
  147:     fields may be list-valued (from `ResearchFrame.to_anchor_protocol`); each
  148:     element is tokenized. A clinical PICO protocol carries none of them, so
  149:     this extension does not change PICO behavior.
  150:     """
  151:     bag: set[str] = set()
  152:     # Legacy clinical PICO anchors (string-valued). Unchanged.
  153:     for field in (
  154:         "research_question", "population", "intervention",
  155:         "comparator", "outcome",
  156:     ):
  157:         val = protocol.get(field) or ""
  158:         bag |= _tokenize(str(val))
  159:     # I-meta-005 Phase 1: field-agnostic frame anchors (list-valued). Skipped
  160:     # gracefully when absent (clinical PICO protocols), so OFF is unchanged.
  161:     for field in (
  162:         "entities", "relations", "metrics", "comparators", "constraints",
  163:     ):
  164:         val = protocol.get(field)
  165:         if isinstance(val, (list, tuple, set)):
  166:             for item in val:
  167:                 bag |= _tokenize(str(item))
  168:         elif val:
  169:             bag |= _tokenize(str(val))
  170:     return bag
  171: 
  172: 
  173: def validate_amplified_queries(
  174:     amplified: list[str],
  175:     protocol: dict[str, Any],
  176:     *,
  177:     floor: Optional[float] = None,
  178:     always_keep_anchor: bool = True,
  179: ) -> ValidationResult:
  180:     """Drop amplified queries that drift off the scope protocol.
  181: 
  182:     Args:
  183:         amplified: Raw output from query amplifier — plain string queries.
  184:         protocol: Dict form of protocol.json, OR any dict with the
  185:             fields research_question / intervention / population / outcome.
  186:         floor: Minimum Jaccard similarity (tokens-vs-anchor-tokens) to
  187:             keep a query. Default: PG_AMPLIFIER_SCOPE_FLOOR env var,
  188:             fallback 0.15.
  189:         always_keep_anchor: When True, the verbatim research_question is
  190:             always kept even if its own Jaccard is below floor (which
  191:             can happen for very short questions). Default True.
  192: 
  193:     Returns:
  194:         ValidationResult with `kept` (queries that passed), `dropped`
  195:         (tuples with reason), and `anchor_tokens_used` for debugging.
  196:     """
  197:     if floor is None:
  198:         floor = float(os.getenv("PG_AMPLIFIER_SCOPE_FLOOR", "0.15"))
  199: 
  200:     # BB-001 (#1171): default `jaccard` = byte-identical OFF; the Gate-B slate
  201:     # sets `containment` so short on-topic queries clear the floor. The gate is
  202:     # KEPT either way (off-anchor queries still fail) — only the MEASURE changes.
  203:     sim_name, sim_fn = _select_sim_measure()
  204: 
  205:     anchor_tokens = _build_anchor_tokens(protocol)
  206:     anchor_tokens_sorted = sorted(anchor_tokens)
  207: 
  208:     research_question = (protocol.get("research_question") or "").strip()
  209: 
  210:     kept: list[str] = []
  211:     dropped: list[tuple[str, float, str]] = []
  212:     seen: set[str] = set()
  213: 
  214:     # Dedupe while preserving order
  215:     unique_amplified: list[str] = []
  216:     for q in amplified:
  217:         norm = (q or "").strip().lower()
  218:         if norm and norm not in seen:
  219:             seen.add(norm)
  220:             unique_amplified.append(q.strip())
  221: 
  222:     for q in unique_amplified:
  223:         q_tokens = _tokenize(q)
  224:         if not q_tokens:
  225:             dropped.append((q, 0.0, "empty_after_tokenization"))
  226:             continue
  227:         sim = sim_fn(q_tokens, anchor_tokens)
  228:         if sim >= floor:
  229:             kept.append(q)
  230:         else:
  231:             # BB-001 (#1171): on the default jaccard path the reason string is
  232:             # BYTE-IDENTICAL to the pre-fix value; the measure suffix is added
  233:             # only when a non-default measure (containment) is active.
  234:             _reason = f"below_scope_floor_{floor:.2f}"
  235:             if sim_name != "jaccard":
  236:                 _reason = f"{_reason}_{sim_name}"
  237:             dropped.append((q, sim, _reason))
  238: 
  239:     # Safety net: always keep the verbatim research_question, even if
  240:     # its own similarity was below floor (happens for very short PICO
  241:     # questions like "Semaglutide efficacy?").
  242:     if always_keep_anchor and research_question:
  243:         if research_question not in kept:
  244:             kept.insert(0, research_question)
  245: 
  246:     logger.info(
  247:         "[scope_validator] measure=%s floor=%.2f kept=%d dropped=%d (anchor_tokens=%d)",
  248:         sim_name, floor, len(kept), len(dropped), len(anchor_tokens),
  249:     )
  250:     if dropped:
  251:         sample = dropped[:3]
  252:         for q, sim, reason in sample:
  253:             logger.debug(
  254:                 "[scope_validator] DROP q=%r sim=%.3f reason=%s",
  255:                 q[:80], sim, reason,
  256:             )
  257: 
  258:     return ValidationResult(
  259:         kept=kept,
  260:         dropped=dropped,
  261:         anchor_tokens_used=anchor_tokens_sorted,
  262:     )

   34: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   35: # BB-001 — scope-validator containment vs jaccard
   36: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   37: 
   38: def _wide_anchor_protocol() -> dict:
   39:     """A ~30-token anchor (research_question + PICO) — the size that punishes short
   40:     on-topic queries under symmetric Jaccard (tiny intersection / huge union)."""
   41:     return {
   42:         "research_question": (
   43:             "To what extent will artificial intelligence and automation technologies "
   44:             "displace or transform jobs across the labor market over the next decade, "
   45:             "and what does the empirical economics literature conclude about net "
   46:             "employment effects and wage polarization in advanced economies?"
   47:         ),
   48:         "population": "workers in advanced economies",
   49:         "intervention": "artificial intelligence automation",
   50:         "outcome": "employment wages displacement",
   51:     }
   52: 
   53: 
   54: # Eight SHORT (4-6 token) on-topic queries — each shares a few anchor terms but its
   55: # union with the 30-token anchor is huge, so jaccard sits far under any sane floor.
   56: _SHORT_ONTOPIC = [
   57:     "automation employment effects",
   58:     "artificial intelligence labor market",
   59:     "wage polarization advanced economies",
   60:     "job displacement automation decade",
   61:     "net employment effects automation",
   62:     "labor market transformation technology",
   63:     "economics literature automation jobs",
   64:     "ai workers displacement wages",
   65: ]
   66: 
   67: 
   68: def test_bb001_containment_keeps_short_ontopic_where_jaccard_drops(monkeypatch):
   69:     """At the legacy code-default floor 0.15 (the forensic's chokepoint: "floor=0.15 kept=5
   70:     dropped=35"), symmetric jaccard drops the short on-topic queries (all score 0.067-0.143 < 0.15
   71:     against the 28-token anchor) while containment keeps them. Funnel delta: jaccard <=2 kept,
   72:     containment >=7 kept — the #1 retrieval-breadth chokepoint widened."""
   73:     proto = _wide_anchor_protocol()
   74:     floor = 0.15  # the legacy code default — the exact floor the forensic recorded the collapse at
   75: 
   76:     monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", "jaccard")
   77:     jac = validate_amplified_queries(list(_SHORT_ONTOPIC), proto, floor=floor)
   78:     # research_question is always prepended (always_keep_anchor); count only the 8 amplified.
   79:     jac_kept = [q for q in jac.kept if q in _SHORT_ONTOPIC]
   80: 
   81:     monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", "containment")
   82:     con = validate_amplified_queries(list(_SHORT_ONTOPIC), proto, floor=floor)
   83:     con_kept = [q for q in con.kept if q in _SHORT_ONTOPIC]
   84: 
   85:     assert len(jac_kept) <= 2, f"jaccard should drop most short on-topic queries, kept {jac_kept}"
   86:     assert len(con_kept) >= 7, f"containment should keep short on-topic queries, kept {con_kept}"
   87: 
   88: 
   89: def test_bb001_off_default_is_jaccard_byte_identical(monkeypatch):
   90:     """Unset PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE == explicit jaccard == legacy behaviour (kept/dropped identical)."""
   91:     proto = _wide_anchor_protocol()
   92:     monkeypatch.delenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", raising=False)
   93:     default = validate_amplified_queries(list(_SHORT_ONTOPIC), proto, floor=0.08)
   94:     monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SCOPE_SIM_MEASURE", "jaccard")
   95:     explicit = validate_amplified_queries(list(_SHORT_ONTOPIC), proto, floor=0.08)
   96:     assert default.kept == explicit.kept
   97:     # OFF reason string carries NO measure suffix (byte-identical legacy reason).
   98:     assert all(r.startswith("below_scope_floor_") and not r.endswith("jaccard")
   99:                for _q, _s, r in default.dropped)

  123: def _install_serper_pages(monkeypatch, pages: dict[int, list[str]]):
  124:     calls: list[int] = []
  125: 
  126:     def _fake(query, per_page, page, headers):
  127:         calls.append(page)

  137: def test_bb002_stop_on_zero_new_continues_past_short_page(monkeypatch):
  138:     """With the flag ON, a sub-per_page page that adds NEW urls does NOT stop the loop."""
  139:     monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_STOP_ON_ZERO_NEW", "1")
  140:     monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_TOTAL_PER_QUERY", "60")
  141:     # page 1: only 5 urls (< per_page 20) but all NEW -> must continue; page 2: 8 more NEW.
  142:     calls = _install_serper_pages(monkeypatch, {
  143:         1: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(5)],
  144:         2: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(5, 13)],
  145:         3: [],  # zero new -> stop
  146:     })
  147:     out = lr._serper_search("q", num=20)
  148:     assert calls == [1, 2, 3], f"expected to page past the short page, got {calls}"
  149:     assert len(out) == 13
  150:

  152: def test_bb002_stop_on_zero_new_stops_on_duplicate_page(monkeypatch):
  153:     """A page that adds 0 NEW (all duplicates) stops the loop even with budget remaining."""
  154:     monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_STOP_ON_ZERO_NEW", "1")
  155:     monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_TOTAL_PER_QUERY", "200")
  156:     monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SERPER_MAX_PAGES", "5")
  157:     calls = _install_serper_pages(monkeypatch, {
  158:         1: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(20)],
  159:         2: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(20)],  # all duplicates -> 0 new -> stop
  160:         3: [f"https://x/{i}" for i in range(40, 60)],  # never reached
  161:     })
  162:     out = lr._serper_search("q", num=20)
  163:     assert calls == [1, 2], f"duplicate page should stop the loop, got {calls}"

  192: def test_bb003_cursor_paging_accumulates_past_25(monkeypatch):
  193:     """With per_page=200 + max_pages>1, the cursor loop accumulates across pages (> the legacy 25)."""
  194:     monkeypatch.setenv("PG_OPENALEX_PER_PAGE", "200")
  195:     monkeypatch.setenv("PG_OPENALEX_MAX_PAGES", "3")
  196:     seen_params: list[dict] = []
  197:     pages = {
  198:         "*": {"results": _make_oa_works(0, 200), "meta": {"next_cursor": "c2"}},
  199:         "c2": {"results": _make_oa_works(200, 200), "meta": {"next_cursor": "c3"}},
  200:         "c3": {"results": _make_oa_works(400, 50), "meta": {"next_cursor": None}},
  201:     }
  202: 
  203:     def _fake_get_json(url, params=None):
  204:         seen_params.append(dict(params or {}))
  205:         return pages.get((params or {}).get("cursor"), {"results": [], "meta": {}})
  206: 
  207:     monkeypatch.setattr(db, "_http_get_json", _fake_get_json)
  208:     # limit=450 so the loop must consume all 3 cursor pages (200+200+50) to accumulate past 25.
  209:     out = db.openalex_search("automation labor", limit=450)
  210:     assert len(out) == 450, f"cursor loop should accumulate across pages, got {len(out)}"
  211:     assert len(out) > 25, "BB-003: must accumulate well past the legacy 25/query single-page cap"
  212:     # per_page=200 sent (the OpenAlex max), and the cursor param threaded across all 3 pages.
  213:     assert all(p["per_page"] == 200 for p in seen_params)
  214:     assert seen_params[0]["cursor"] == "*"
  215:     assert len(seen_params) == 3
  216:     assert [p["cursor"] for p in seen_params] == ["*", "c2", "c3"]
  217: 
  218: 
  219: def test_bb003_off_default_single_page_no_cursor_byte_identical(monkeypatch):
  220:     """OFF (per_page unset=25, max_pages unset=1): exactly the legacy single 25-cap request, no cursor."""
  221:     monkeypatch.delenv("PG_OPENALEX_PER_PAGE", raising=False)
  222:     monkeypatch.delenv("PG_OPENALEX_MAX_PAGES", raising=False)
  223:     seen_params: list[dict] = []
  224: 
  225:     def _fake_get_json(url, params=None):
  226:         seen_params.append(dict(params or {}))
  227:         return {"results": _make_oa_works(0, 25), "meta": {"next_cursor": "c2"}}
  228: 
  229:     monkeypatch.setattr(db, "_http_get_json", _fake_get_json)

  231:     assert len(seen_params) == 1, "OFF must issue exactly one page"
  232:     assert "cursor" not in seen_params[0], "OFF request must NOT carry a cursor param (byte-identical)"
  233:     assert seen_params[0]["per_page"] == 25  # max(1, min(100, 25))

  253:         pass
  254: 
  255:     def __enter__(self):
  256:         return self
  257: 
  258:     def __exit__(self, *a):
  259:         return False

  263:     traced: list[dict] = []
  264: 
  265:     def _fake_get(self, url, params=None, headers=None):
  266:         return _FakeResp(200, payload)
  267: 
  268:     monkeypatch.setattr(_FakeClient, "get", _fake_get, raising=False)
  269:     monkeypatch.setattr(lr.httpx, "Client", lambda *a, **k: _FakeClient())
  270: 
  271:     def _fake_trace(tool_name, **kw):
  272:         if tool_name == "s2":
  273:             traced.append({"tool": tool_name, **kw})
  274: 
  275:     monkeypatch.setattr(lr, "_trace_tool", _fake_trace)
  276:     monkeypatch.setattr(lr, "_trace_query", lambda *a, **k: None)
  277:     return traced

  330: # BB-006 — STORM URL-ONLY harvest (faithfulness contract)
  331: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

  333: def _storm_out_with(n: int) -> dict:
  334:     """A STORM result carrying web_results URLs AND synthesized text that must NEVER be harvested."""
  335:     return {
  336:         "storm_conversations": [{"q": "interview q", "a": "interview answer text"}],
  337:         "storm_outline": ["section 1", "section 2"],
  338:         "web_results": [
  339:             {"url": f"https://storm/{i}", "title": f"title {i}",
  340:              "snippet": f"SYNTHESIZED-SNIPPET-{i}-must-not-be-evidence"}
  341:             for i in range(n)
  342:         ],
  343:         "academic_results": [{"url": f"https://storm-ac/{i}", "title": "ac", "snippet": "ac snip"}
  344:                              for i in range(3)],
  345:         # synthesized fields that must NEVER appear in the harvest:
  346:         "answer": "STORM SYNTHESIZED ANSWER — this is a paraphrase and must not be evidence",
  347:         "key_findings": ["STORM KEY FINDING that is an LLM paraphrase"],
  348:     }
  349:

  351: def test_bb006_harvest_storm_urls_returns_only_urls():
  352:     """harvest_storm_urls returns ONLY web_results/academic_results URLs — never synthesized text."""
  353:     out = harvest_storm_urls(_storm_out_with(478), cap=200)
  354:     assert len(out) == 200  # capped
  355:     # Every returned item is a fetchable URL from the result streams.
  356:     assert all(u.startswith("https://storm") for u in out)
  357:     # The HARD contract: no synthesized STORM text leaked into the harvest.
  358:     blob = " ".join(out)
  359:     assert "SYNTHESIZED-SNIPPET" not in blob
  360:     assert "SYNTHESIZED ANSWER" not in blob
  361:     assert "KEY FINDING" not in blob
  362:     assert "interview answer" not in blob
  363:

  368:     assert len(out) == 53                 # 50 web + 3 academic, all distinct

  377: def test_bb006_storm_snippet_never_becomes_direct_quote():
  378:     """A STORM seed URL flows as a URL-only candidate: harvest never carries the snippet as a quote.
  379: 
  380:     (The seed re-fetch makes direct_quote the verbatim FETCHED span; the harvest output is a bare
  381:     URL string — there is no field through which the synthesized snippet could ride as evidence.)

  984: def apply_journal_only_for_slug(slug: str) -> bool:
  985:     """DETERMINISTICALLY set/clear the journal_only runtime flag for ONE benchmark slug.
  986: 
  987:     Sets ``PG_SOURCE_RESTRICTION_JOURNAL_ONLY=1`` iff ``slug`` is a journal_only benchmark slug
  988:     (``JOURNAL_ONLY_BENCHMARK_SLUGS``); otherwise it REMOVES the flag from the env so a value
  989:     left over from a prior journal_only slug in the SAME process (e.g. the ``--all`` loop, or a
  990:     conservative ``.env`` default) can NEVER carry into a non-journal slug. Returns True iff the
  991:     flag was set ON for this slug.
  992: 
  993:     This is the per-question seam (mirrors how the slate is applied per ``run_gate_b_query``): it
  994:     runs INSIDE ``run_gate_b_query`` so the flag is correct for exactly the question being run,
  995:     NOT added to the always-on global ``_FULL_CAPABILITY_BENCHMARK_SLATE`` (which would blanket-
  996:     activate journal_only for every workforce query and kill the generic T3 path). The downstream
  997:     consumer (``run_honest_sweep_r3.run_one_query`` -> ``_jo_active`` -> ``journal_only_active``)
  998:     reads ``JOURNAL_ONLY_FLAG`` from the env at run time AND requires the protocol's
  999:     ``source_restriction: journal_only``, so setting it here before the ``run_one_query`` call is
 1000:     what makes journal_only fire for the journal-only slug only. Default non-journal runs are
 1001:     byte-identical (the flag is removed, not set).
 1002:     """

 1005:         return True
 1006:     os.environ.pop(JOURNAL_ONLY_FLAG, None)
 1007:     return False

  288: def filter_to_citeable(rows: Iterable[Any], sidecar: Mapping[str, Any]) -> FilterResult:
  289:     """Partition evidence rows OR CorpusSource objects into citeable / excluded.
  290: 
  291:     Works on both ``evidence_row`` dicts (``source_url``/``tier`` keys) and
  292:     ``CorpusSource`` dataclasses (``.url``/``.tier``). Excluded rows are recorded

  299:         if ok:
  300:             out.citeable.append(row)
  301:         else:
  302:             out.excluded.append({"url": url, "reason": reason})
  303:     return out

  337: def make_feature_telemetry(feature: str, **extra: Any) -> dict[str, Any]:
  338:     """I-ready-005 (#1076): default per-feature FIRING telemetry surfaced to the manifest so the operator
  339:     can prove a forced-ON benchmark feature actually fired. firing_status: not_enabled ->
  340:     attempted_empty (block ran) -> fired (produced output) / error. ``extra`` adds feature-specific
  341:     count keys (e.g. questions_added, urls_discovered).
  342: 
  343:     I-ready-016 (#1086): the key is ``firing_status`` (NOT ``status``) — it is a per-feature firing
  344:     state stamped under manifest['<feature>'], NOT the manifest's own pipeline ``status``. The rename
  345:     keeps the manifest-status authoritativeness contract (test_manifest_contract) from mistaking a
  346:     feature firing-state for a manifest status."""
  347:     base = {"feature": feature, "enabled": False, "fired": False, "firing_status": "not_enabled"}
  348:     base.update(extra)
  349:     return base
  350: 
  351: 
  352: def feature_firing_warning(telemetry: dict[str, Any]) -> str | None:
  353:     """Return a LOUD warning string if a feature was force-ENABLED but did NOT fire (the silent-degrade
  354:     the operator's no-downgrade directive forbids), else None. Non-gating — advisory surface."""
  355:     if telemetry.get("enabled") and not telemetry.get("fired"):
  356:         return (
  357:             f"{telemetry.get('feature')} was force-ENABLED but did NOT fire "
  358:             f"(firing_status={telemetry.get('firing_status')}) — verify the run before trusting it"
  359:         )
  360:     return None
  361: 
  362: 
  363: def retrieval_fetch_disclosure(fetched: int, failed: int, total: int) -> str:
  364:     """FIX-A10 (#1100): one reader-facing Methods line disclosing the retrieval fetch outcome, so a
  365:     run whose corpus was upstream-starved (e.g. drb_72: 26/155 fetched, 129 failed/timeout) does not
  366:     look complete. Pure; no I/O."""
  367:     return (
  368:         f"Retrieval fetch outcome: {int(fetched)} of {int(total)} candidate sources fetched; "
  369:         f"{int(failed)} failed or timed out.\n"
  370:     )
  371: 
  372: 
  373: def retrieval_failure_warning(fetched: int, failed: int, total: int, warn_rate: float) -> str | None:
  374:     """FIX-A10 (#1100): LOUD warning string when the fetch-failure rate >= ``warn_rate`` (env-driven,
  375:     LAW VI), else None. Silent upstream starvation is the no-downgrade directive's high-harm case."""
  376:     total = int(total)
  377:     if total <= 0:
  378:         return None
  379:     rate = int(failed) / total
  380:     if rate < warn_rate:
  381:         return None
  382:     return (
  383:         f"{int(failed)}/{total} candidate fetches failed or timed out "
  384:         f"({rate:.0%} >= {warn_rate:.0%} PG_RETRIEVAL_FAILURE_WARN_RATE) — corpus is "
  385:         f"upstream-starved; coverage may be degraded"
  386:     )
  387: 
  388: 
  389: def quantified_degradation_disclosure(telemetry: dict[str, Any] | None) -> str:
  390:     """FIX-A9 (#1100): reader-facing '## Capability disclosures' block IFF quantified-analysis was
  391:     ENABLED but produced no verified output (fired-equivalent = verified_sentences>0, the same signal
  392:     _normalize_quantified_telemetry uses). Returns '' when not degraded (no report change). Pure."""
  393:     if not isinstance(telemetry, dict):
  394:         return ""
  395:     if not telemetry.get("enabled"):
  396:         return ""
  397:     if int(telemetry.get("verified_sentences", 0) or 0) > 0:
  398:         return ""
  399:     why = telemetry.get("firing_status") or telemetry.get("error") or "no verified quantified output"
  400:     extracted = int(telemetry.get("sourced_numbers_extracted", 0) or 0)
  401:     return (
  402:         f"\n## Capability disclosures\n"
  403:         f"Quantified trade-off analysis was ENABLED but did not contribute to this report "
  404:         f"({why}); {extracted} sourced numbers were extracted but not modeled into a verified "
  405:         f"quantified comparison.\n"
  406:     )
  407: 
  408: 
  409: # FL-05 (#1124): a force-enabled discovery feature with one of these firing states silently
  410: # degraded the run to the Serper/S2 baseline (block ran but produced nothing / errored).
  411: _FL05_DEGRADED_FIRING: frozenset[str] = frozenset({"attempted_empty", "error"})
  412: 
  413: 
  414: def compute_run_health_gate(
  415:     discovery_telemetries: list[dict[str, Any]],
  416:     *,
  417:     unified_status: str,
  418:     gate_on: bool,
  419:     storm_min_effective_queries: int = 0,
  420: ) -> dict[str, Any]:
  421:     """FL-05 (#1124): run-health backstop DECISION (pure, no I/O — testable). A FORCE-ENABLED
  422:     discovery feature (``enabled`` True) whose ``firing_status`` is in ``_FL05_DEGRADED_FIRING``
  423:     means the run silently fell back to the baseline. Returns the observability fields ALWAYS, plus
  424:     an ``override_status`` of ``abort_discovery_degraded`` IFF ``gate_on`` AND at least one degraded
  425:     force-enabled feature AND the run is otherwise success-bound. NEVER overrides a partial_/abort_/
  426:     error_ status (those are more specific) — only a would-be ``success``. This promotes
  427:     ``feature_firing_warning`` from advisory to gating (CANARY-01 is the pre-spend gate; FL-05 is the
  428:     mid/post-run regression backstop).
  429: 
  430:     I-fetch-002 (#1168): STORM UNDER-fire (post-validator collapse). The classic FL-05 path above only
  431:     catches a TOTAL no-fire (firing_status attempted_empty/error). A run where STORM force-on FIRED
  432:     (firing_status=fired) but produced FEWER than ``storm_min_effective_queries`` EFFECTIVE queries
  433:     (``effective_query_count``) is a thin-corpus collapse that would otherwise ship green. Such a
  434:     feature is ADDED to the degraded set (same abort path, same release-withhold). The check requires
  435:     ``effective_query_count`` to be PRESENT and not None (never treats an absent field as 0), so a
  436:     feature that does not publish the count — e.g. agentic, which publishes urls_discovered — never
  437:     trips it. ``storm_min_effective_queries`` defaults to 0 (disabled): with the default, ``count < 0``
  438:     never fires, so every pre-existing caller/test is byte-unchanged. Discovery-health only (no
  439:     faithfulness path touched)."""
  440:     degraded = [
  441:         t for t in discovery_telemetries
  442:         if t.get("enabled") and t.get("firing_status") in _FL05_DEGRADED_FIRING
  443:     ]
  444:     # I-fetch-002 (#1168): UNDER-fire — fired but below the effective-query floor. Mutually exclusive
  445:     # with the TOTAL no-fire set above (firing_status=fired vs attempted_empty/error), so no double-count.
  446:     under_fired = [
  447:         t for t in discovery_telemetries
  448:         if (
  449:             t.get("enabled")
  450:             and t.get("firing_status") == "fired"
  451:             and t.get("effective_query_count") is not None
  452:             and int(t.get("effective_query_count")) < storm_min_effective_queries
  453:         )
  454:     ]
  455:     all_degraded = degraded + under_fired
  456:     override = (
  457:         "abort_discovery_degraded"
  458:         if (gate_on and all_degraded and unified_status == "success")
  459:         else None
  460:     )
  461:     return {
  462:         "discovery_llm_degraded": bool(all_degraded),
  463:         "discovery_rounds_on_fallback": len(all_degraded),
  464:         "degraded_features": [
  465:             {"feature": t.get("feature"), "firing_status": t.get("firing_status")}
  466:             for t in degraded
  467:         ] + [
  468:             {
  469:                 "feature": t.get("feature"),
  470:                 "firing_status": "under_fired",
  471:                 "effective_query_count": int(t.get("effective_query_count")),
  472:             }
  473:             for t in under_fired
  474:         ],
  475:         "override_status": override,
  476:     }
  477: 
  478:
