  194: def _resp_content_len(resp: Any) -> int:
  195:     """Best-effort byte length of an httpx response body for telemetry.
  196: 
  197:     Returns 0 when the response object lacks a measurable ``content`` (e.g. a
  198:     lightweight test double). NEVER raises — record-only telemetry must not
  199:     depend on the response's concrete shape.
  200:     """
  201:     try:
  202:         content = getattr(resp, "content", None)
  203:         return len(content) if content else 0
  204:     except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — telemetry must never break retrieval
  205:         return 0

  218: def _serper_fetch_page(
  219:     query: str, per_page: int, page: int, headers: dict[str, str]
  220: ) -> tuple[list[dict[str, Any]], bool, float, int, str]:
  221:     """FX-17 (#1126): fetch ONE Serper page. Returns (items, ok, latency_ms, resp_bytes, error).
  222:     Byte-identical to the legacy single call when page==1 (no `page` key in the payload)."""
  223:     payload: dict[str, Any] = {"q": query, "num": per_page}
  224:     if page > 1:
  225:         payload["page"] = page
  226:     _t0 = time.time()
  227:     try:
  228:         with httpx.Client(timeout=DEFAULT_HTTP_TIMEOUT) as c:
  229:             r = c.post(SERPER_ENDPOINT, json=payload, headers=headers)
  230:         _latency_ms = (time.time() - _t0) * 1000.0
  231:         if r.status_code != 200:
  232:             return [], False, _latency_ms, _resp_content_len(r), f"HTTP {r.status_code}"
  233:         organic = (r.json().get("organic", []) or [])
  234:         items = [
  235:             {"url": it.get("link", ""), "title": it.get("title", ""),
  236:              "snippet": it.get("snippet", ""), "source": "serper"}
  237:             for it in organic
  238:         ]
  239:         return items, True, _latency_ms, _resp_content_len(r), ""
  240:     except Exception as exc:
  241:         return [], False, (time.time() - _t0) * 1000.0, 0, str(exc)

    2: Pre-fetch off-topic filter — HONEST-REBUILD Phase 2d.

    6: clearly unrelated to the research question.
    7: 
    8: WHY THIS EXISTS (PG_LB_SA_02_CONTENT_AUDIT Section E-03):
    9: - The pre-rebuild pipeline fetched every search result, extracted
   10:   evidence, then filtered off-topic evidence during synthesis.
   11: - The legacy PG_OFFTOPIC_THRESHOLD=0.15 was so low that near-zero-
   12:   similarity evidence (e.g., Japan health insurance general articles
   13:   when the query was semaglutide CV risk) survived.
   14: - The "risk axis retained below threshold" path further defeated
   15:   tightening attempts because its floor was pinned at 0.15.
   16: 
   17: PHASE 2D APPROACH:
   18: - Filter snippets BEFORE fetch using a looser threshold
   19:   (PG_OFFTOPIC_PREFETCH_THRESHOLD, default 0.25).

   21:   (PG_OFFTOPIC_THRESHOLD, default 0.35).

   62:   "frontier_best_practice": "Modern frontier practice for clinical question scoping has moved decisively away from the brittle regex extraction this gate uses, and \u2014 more importantly \u2014 establishes that broad clinical lit-review questions should NOT be PICO-narrowed or refused at all.\n\n1) PICO is the WRONG frame for these questions. The three failing questions (metal-ion modulation for CVD; gut microbiota/probiotics/prebiotics for CRC; Parkinson's staging + DBS daily-life support) are exactly PCC-shaped review questions: they have a clear Population (CVD patients; people at CRC risk; Parkinson's/DBS patients) and Concept (metal-ion modulation; microbiota modulation; DBS support), but no single narrow drug \"Intervention\" the regex can grab. The gate's \"both anchors missing -> hard reject\" is the precise anti-pattern PCC was designed to avoid. Sources: systematicliteraturereviews.com/pcc-framework/ ; guides.atsu.edu/scopingreviews/protocol ; libguides.jcu.edu.au/scoping/define.\n\n2) Extraction itself should be LLM-assisted, not regex, when you do extract structure: GPT-4/Claude-3 reach ~80% PICO accuracy (AlpaPICO, JAMIA 2025, npj Digital Medicine 2025), vs the keyword regex here that only knows a fixed GLP-1/oncology drug list and a fixed demographic list. arxiv.org/abs/2409.09704 (AlpaPICO); academic.oup.com/jamia/article/32/6/1071/8126534 ; nature.com/articles/s41746-025-01840-7. codex
**Findings**

P1: The STORM URL seed lane breaks the hard ~1000 fetch envelope. The slate says this cluster must “NEVER raise total FETCH” and keeps the four lanes at `800 + 100 + 60 + 40 = 1000`, but it also adds `PG_STORM_URL_FETCH_CAP=60` as a separate additive lane in [run_gate_b.py](C:/POLARIS/scripts/dr_benchmark/run_gate_b.py:593). That cap is actually fetched after the existing lanes via `run_live_retrieval(seed_only=True)` in [run_honest_sweep_r3.py](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:3404). Net effect: Gate-B can fetch up to ~1060, contradicting the no-overshoot contract and the local fix design’s “do NOT push total FETCH >~1000” constraint. Make STORM URLs compete inside an existing lane/cap, or reduce another fetch lane by the STORM fetch allowance.

P2: The offline smoke is mostly behavioral and passed, but BB-005 only tests `harvest_agentic_urls` directly. It does not prove the run-level decouple that matters: `urls_discovered_total` can rise to 800 while the seed list sent to `run_live_retrieval(seed_only=True)` remains capped at 100. The code appears to do this, but the smoke does not lock it.
